  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a70aec5a-db61-444b-91b7-4874e2457fe6'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9865733060050680870">Teens control the fate of America in the fourth and final book in the New York Times bestselling Unwind dystology by Neal Shusterman.<br/><br/>Proactive Citizenry, the company that created Cam from the parts of unwound teens, has a plan: to mass produce rewound teens like Cam for military purposes. And below the surface of that horror lies another shocking level of intrigue: Proacti</span>
  <span id="freeText9865733060050680870" style="display:none">Teens control the fate of America in the fourth and final book in the New York Times bestselling Unwind dystology by Neal Shusterman.<br /><br />Proactive Citizenry, the company that created Cam from the parts of unwound teens, has a plan: to mass produce rewound teens like Cam for military purposes. And below the surface of that horror lies another shocking level of intrigue: Proactive Citizenry has been suppressing technology that could make unwinding completely unnecessary. As Conner, Risa, and Lev uncover these startling secrets, enraged teens begin to march on Washington to demand justice and a better future.<br /><br />But more trouble is brewing. Starkey’s group of storked teens is growing more powerful and militant with each new recruit. And if they have their way, they’ll burn the harvest camps to the ground and put every adult in them before a firing squad—which could destroy any chance America has for a peaceful future.</span>

<div id="review_709810036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/709810036" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/709810036?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who liked The Knife of Never Letting Go, Angelfall</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=quit-crying-robin">quit-crying-robin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer709810036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10500313880741801570">Reread with a few friends at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> in <s>January</s>Feb 2016, we got sidetracked, it happens.<br/><br/>This is still my favorite completed YA series to date. The entire thing is awesome and even the second time through everything held up so well.<br/><br/><b>Overall Series 4.5 “Nice Socks” Stars<br/><br/><a> Unwind</a> 5 Stars<br/><a> Unwholly </a> 4.5 Stars <br/><a>Unsouled</a> 4 Stars<br/><br/>Undivided 5 Stars </b><br/><br/>I thought, I couldn’t be shocked anymore….<br/>I thought, nothing Neal Shusterman says or does will surprise me now…<br/>I thought, there was nothing more</span>
  <span id="freeText10500313880741801570" style="display:none">Reread with a few friends at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> in <s>January</s>Feb 2016, we got sidetracked, it happens.<br /><br />This is still my favorite completed YA series to date. The entire thing is awesome and even the second time through everything held up so well.<br /><br /><b>Overall Series 4.5 “Nice Socks” Stars<br /><br /><a> Unwind</a> 5 Stars<br /><a> Unwholly </a> 4.5 Stars <br /><a>Unsouled</a> 4 Stars<br /><br />Undivided 5 Stars </b><br /><br />I thought, I couldn’t be shocked anymore….<br />I thought, nothing Neal Shusterman says or does will surprise me now…<br />I thought, there was nothing more horrible than the things I’ve already seen in this series...<br />I thought, I knew who to hate and who to love in the story….<br />I thought, I was prepared….<br /><b>I was wrong. So…so…wrong</b><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “Tools are neither demonic nor divine. It’s all about who wields them.”</b>
</blockquote><br />I’ve been severely disappointed with dystopian novels lately. They all seem to start out strong and then just dwindle or they are exactly the same as everything else out there <s>Aligent, Requiem</s>. However, the Unwind series is a true sparkling diamond in a sea of cubic zirconia. Neal Shusterman lines up all the pieces in the story, sets the tumblers in motion and much like a game of Plinko I had no idea where the pieces would finally come to rest. Undivided is an AMAZING wrap up to the Unwind series. <b>This is the series you recommend first when someone asks if you know of any good Dystopian or YA novels.</b><br /><br />Just like the other books in the series it is told in the multiple PoV fashion mostly from the viewpoints of Connor, Risa, Lev and Cam but also there are others from Hayden, Argent, Una , Starkey and more peppered in. It is amazing the full scope of the story you feel you are getting from seeing it from all of these perspectives. The villains are so powerfully portrayed, I really felt like I understood their motives and some of their craziness.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Starkey believes he is invincible. He believes he is more than just destined for greatness, but that greatness is owed to him, and every one of these “victories” makes him believe it more and more. The Stork Lord. Hayden’s epithet is more on-target then even he realizes, for Starkey truly does see himself as royalty reaching for divinity. A chosen one with the pride and privilege of a god.</i>
</b><br /><br />The heroes are portrayed equally as honestly with all of their attributes and faults on display as well. No one is perfect but everyone is trying to do the best they can with what they have.<br /><br />Conner is not the same troubled boy he was in Unwind. He has really grown up over that last two years of running. He is easy to like and I am so happy that he and Risa were finally together again for the majority of this book. The love story between them is truly fantastic, well developed and beautiful. There has been no insta love here. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><i>But Risa can’t leave yet. Not without saying those words that come so hard, but mean more than anything now. The words she fears she may never get to say again. “Connor, I—”<br />“Don’t!” Connor’s lower lip quivers. “Because if you say it, it’ll sound too much like a good-bye, and I don’t think I could take that.” <br />And so Risa doesn’t speak it aloud, but it’s there between them, more powerful than anything either of them can say. She leans over, kisses him, then hurries to the door where Argent waits, his half-face red with fright. It’s just as they leave that Connor breaks down and utters the words he couldn’t bear to hear himself. “I love you, Risa,” he says. “Every last part of me.” *sobs, wipes tears from cheeks* </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There are a lot of really horrible disturbing moments in this book, but they are written in such a way that while yes, they are still disturbing I couldn’t help but read on, enthralled by the story. There are also as many truly touching heartfelt moments. I teared up more than once with the emotion of those moments. Even characters I thought I could not feel any sympathy toward somehow were able to elicit very confused feeling from me. I hated them but the events of a few situations really made me feel all the more sorry for them.<br /><br />A revolution is building but for change to happen a bunch of things will all need to fall into place at the same time. So many issues on the ballot for the election that have to do with unwinding and Proactive Citezenry are ramping up their propaganda campaigns. This is one of the things I really like about these novels, the way that advertising is used to show how different organizations are really promoting the same ideas and really all working for the same organization even though they seem to be promoting different things. It is incredibly smart.<br /><br /><blockquote><b>THE FOLLOWING IS A PAID POLITICAL ADVERTISEMENT <br />DON’T BE FOOLED BY MEASURE F!</b><br /><i> Supporters of the so-called Prevention Initiative claim that it’s all about the protection of at-risk children—but read the fine print! Measure F allows the Juvenile Authority to identify and track incorrigible children for the purpose of unwinding them as soon as they turn thirteen—which will be legal once the Parental Override bill becomes law. Measure G, on the other hand, funds the Juvenile Authority by giving cash incentives for the capture of AWOLs—who have already proven themselves to be menaces to society. No on F! Yes on G! Make the sensible choice!</i><br />-- Paid for by the Alliance for an AWOL-Free Nation</blockquote><br /><br />At the beginning of every section there are also references to actual stories from today that if taken just a little farther to a slight extreme could lead down this road. It is amazing to think that some of the stuff in the book is not that far from reality. There are also some radio broadcasts being put out by Hayden trying to ramp up support. He is slowly exposing Proactive Citizenry and the Juvenile Authority for the monsters they really are a little at a time in hopes that the people will have had enough and join in a single voice. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Y’know, if I wanted to make sure that the Juvenile Authority had greater and greater support, I would trick angry teenagers into blowing themselves up, and then blame the angry teenagers! No mess, no bother. Well, quite a lot of mess, but you get my point.</i>
</b><br /><br />All the little touches of the radio broadcasts, advertisements and articles from today and part of what makes this story so special and gives it just that little extra something.<br /><br />The story ties comes together so well and I really sat on the edge of my seat near the end so worried for all of the characters I love. There are some happy endings, there are some endings and there are some new beginnings. <br /><br />Our heroes Connor, Risa, Lev and Cam will all go to some extraordinary lengths so that no other troubled teen, ward of the state or tithe will ever suffer the fate of running from the law and the threat of being unwound. One of them will risk everything they are just for that hope. I’m sad to leave all these characters behind but I know that this is one of those storied that will stick with me and I will read time and time again throughout my life and get something different from it each time.<br /><br /><b>I don’t read much YA anymore but books like these are why I still bother to read this genre at all.</b> It is the journey that you want to see in a YA novel, but rarely get. The series is complete so no time like the present to jump in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10500313880741801570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

What an amazing way to end an amazing series.<br/><br/>Neal Shusterman, you are a mad genius.</span>

  <span id="freeText4965366239339216246" style="display:none"><u>FINAL REVIEW</u><br>O. M. G. SO MANY. SO MANY FEELS. fjkalsdfjkl; AKA prepare for all of the gifs #sorrynotsorry <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946965.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946966.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946967.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946968.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Neal Shusterman... WHO ARE YOU? Why are you this good?! (these tears are happy tears. also sad tears. just emotional tears. idk)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946969.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Substitute Neal Shusterman</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946970.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like where do I even start with this series? <br><br>First, let's begin with this because this book deserves one: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946971.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946972.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946973.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>We all know that's what you're thinking.</i><br><br>Second, let's continue with one of the main reasons (there are many) why I LOVE this book (and series) so much. <br>1) The characters, both the "heroes" and the "villains." (quotations because there are no such labels in this series YAAAAAS)<br>- All of them are believable &lt;- because they are HUMAN (when I say human, I mean with real emotions with messy lives with real flaws and strengths who are trying to make sense of the world that they are in)<br>- All of them have stories &lt;- which Neal Shusterman beautifully shares and balances -&gt; you connect, get to know, and fall in love with each character<br>- Even the bad guys have stories that you connect with and understand why they do what they do (even as you shudder and get chills all over your body)<br>- The individual matters ... NOT just the main characters or actors or POVs covered by the story, but the "common" everyday invisible civilian/official/AWOL/gardener/parent/person ... and it is BEAUTIFUL<br>- And on and on. aka they are amazing:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946974.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2) The world building and masterful storytelling<br>- the masterful weaving in of tiny stories, tiny parts that are seemingly insignificant, but when brought together, they create something beautiful (do you see what Neal Shusterman did there? re: actual topic covered by the series)<br>- ex: I am reading something and then I realize that it is an ACTUAL, real-life article that can be read -&gt; augments the reading experience and makes the dystopian world that much more realistic and terrifying, but also hopeful (becuz people can be good and awesome) -&gt; it does what fiction is SUPPOSED to do which is supposed to reflect and reveal our own realities, histories, and stories (YES YES YES NEAL SHUSTERMAN YES YES YES)<br>- you literally get sucked into the world and you can't get out of it until like never (whoops) because as you flip or click (like me - shoutout to my computer) the last page, you carry that world and the messages it gives with you as you go about your life (like what fiction is supposed to do!!)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946975.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946977.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>3) The message <br>- You know you've hit the goldmine of a book/series when it not only is fun/amazing/keeps you on the edge of your seat but when it also appeals and challenges your thoughts and empathy and really engages with you as a reader<br>- Also engages with your morality and questions and guides you through your questioning like any good book should do while not giving you all the answers<br>- I love the message(s) in this book so much. It kept me smiling, palpitating, crying, laughing, crying again, and squealing in glee/crying the whole way through because it shows you humanity, both the good and the bad, and the potential for both that we all carry <br><br>4) so much more that I could drone on about but will bore you<br><br>So basic moral of the story (heh), READ THE BOOK. READ THE SERIES. GO GO GO. You've heard me!<br>If you do: you will be the person on the other end of these gifs.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946978.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946979.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And you will be doing this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946980.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946981.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946982.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946983.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946986.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369625ra/14946987.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not that I can read the future or anything. (or can I?)<br><br>My message to this book and Neal Shusterman: FIVE FOR YOU UNDIVIDED/SERIES (aka Glen Coco) FIVE STARS FOR YOU. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432369626ra/14946988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And none for *substitute any dystopian/YA novels that fail hard* BYE.<br><br><u>Update: Feb. 21</u><br>OMG. THE COVER. IT'S TOO MUCH. <div id="review_1031006390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1031006390" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1031006390?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1031006390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5851715399088453496"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-undivided.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415635590i/11822193.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Short review:</b><br/><br/>I am unwinding in the inside.<br/>My thoughts are in a divided state and I can't make myself rewind them. <br/><br/>This story is too powerful for words. <br/><br/>I just know that I LOVE this series.<br/>I know that I love...<br/>I... I know that...<br/>I...<br/>I...<br/>...<br/>...<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>There are very few books so powerful that can follow you into your dreams. That leave an imprint on your soul. That are so dreadful and horrifying, but in the same time so beautiful and completely mesmerising.<br/><br/>And this time around it was true,</span>
  <span id="freeText5851715399088453496" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-undivided.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415635590i/11822193.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Short review:</b><br><br>I am unwinding in the inside.<br>My thoughts are in a divided state and I can't make myself rewind them. <br><br>This story is too powerful for words. <br><br>I just know that I LOVE this series.<br>I know that I love...<br>I... I know that...<br>I...<br>I...<br>...<br>...<br><br><b>Full review:</b><br><br>There are very few books so powerful that can follow you into your dreams. That leave an imprint on your soul. That are so dreadful and horrifying, but in the same time so beautiful and completely mesmerising.<br><br>And this time around it was true, it was not a wish of sorts, not a simple thought that just comes and goes. After reading it (this whole series), I had the more horrifying night ever – dreaming of unwinds and AWOLs, leaping back into consciousness only to be swept away into another desperate dream, where someone would be divided to pieces and I would endlessly run for my life.<br><br>It’s no wonder actually, as I’ve been spending around 4-5 days with the series, so my mind was pretty much overfilled with this story, but still.. I confirm that (indeed) this book has the power to haunt you even in your sleep.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413554578i/11528670.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s hard to get to the end of a series when you love it as much as I loved this one. It pains me to be over with it.<br><br>But truth being told, it was exhausting, emotionally draining! My heart wouldn’t have been able to take any more pain or suspense, and I think that the characters felt just the same.<br><br>Everything came into place. Everything made complete sense. All their small fights had an impact on the world around, but the way it resonated – well, that seemed to be a lot greater than the sum of its parts. They probably never dreamed of achieving this much. They just wanted a chance to… be.<br><br>If the first book was created as a standalone, the last 3 books come hand in hand. You can’t have one without the others, you can’t see the big picture without reading them all. It started as the story of Risa, Lev and Connor. It ended as the story of so many more.<br><br>All those people who didn’t believe in unwinding (/anymore), all those people who needed and wanted things to change, all those people who were guilty in a way or another, all those people that had a handful of letters written in blood, even the world itself was there to watch them take the last steps in this journey – and it was marvellous.<br><br>Without any of them, the story wouldn’t have been the same, the ending wouldn’t have been as great. Their individual fights, their sacrifices, their strength and hope for a better world was what drove them on this path.<br><br>There are not enough words in this world to express the immensity and the beauty of it all.<br><br>I will miss these characters dearly, I feel like knowing them better than I know my own friends and I cared for them so much through this story. They are part of my life now and I refuse to say goodbye.<br><br><b>Conclusion:</b> <br> <blockquote>
<i>I wish I could unwind time so I could experience this book from every possible angle, not passing through the moment, but living it.</i> <br>[adapted from a book quote from Connor] </blockquote><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-undivided.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>* Read the full review <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-undivided.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691049753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11952098856996878240">OH MAN. OH GOD. OH MAN.<br/><br/>I need a couple days to process this. Wow.<br/><br/>I don't know why it took me so long to finally finish this series, but I'm glad I finally got around to it. Because <i>dang</i>, this last book was incredible. Talk about an amazing series finale. It's terrifying, intense, disturbing, but ultimately uplifting. As always, Neal Shusterman's world-building, plotting, and characters are just genius. <br/><br/>Full review coming soon! </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1018620003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16997868410451944912"><a href='https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png' width='350' height='117' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>REVIEW FREE OF SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS.</b><br/><br/><i>Unwind</i> to me has always been known because it's one of the best dystopia series I've ever read. Mainly, it's because its realism is overwhelming - so realistic it's almost painful - and it continued that way throughout the four books.<br/><br/>First, the subject matter in the book is not so far from reality. I'm not saying we're close to parents giving away their children to the authorities so they can have them unwound (split their body parts without kil</span>
  <span id="freeText16997868410451944912" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>REVIEW FREE OF SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS.</b><br><br><i>Unwind</i> to me has always been known because it's one of the best dystopia series I've ever read. Mainly, it's because its realism is overwhelming - so realistic it's almost painful - and it continued that way throughout the four books.<br><br>First, the subject matter in the book is not so far from reality. I'm not saying we're close to parents giving away their children to the authorities so they can have them unwound (split their body parts without killing them). I'm talking more about organ trafficking and such. The way that is portrayed in the book is disturbing to the point of scary.<br><br>My second reason for saying this is one of the most realistic dystopias is because nothing is sugar-coated. The author is not afraid of describing youngsters' deaths and he's also not afraid of having both beloved and hated characters unwound.<br><br>The <i>Unwind</i> world is full with merciless people, selfish people, cynics, monsters (not in the literal sense), and it's so damn <i>human</i>. Our best and worst qualities are present here.<br><br>Furthermore, the realism of the series doesn't extend only to the world - it also goes as far as the character development. Children are forced to mature before they're teenagers, teenagers are forced to abandon their studies and turn into fugitives, 17-year-olds have to learn to be in the head of a rebellion which has the odds to lose, etc.<br><br>That's in general, but our main characters also have to undergo lots of changes. They're clearly not the same they were when the series started. Some lost their innocence, and they're surrounded with darkness. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm talking about Lev, here. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The decisions they make are less childish and more intelligent. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Connor and Risa. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I can speak like that of everyone in the book because we have a complete view of all the events - there are lots of POVs. Worry not, though. <b>All the POVs were well-written and believable.</b><br><br>To add more realism to all, at the beginning of each part of the book came sneak peeks of striking news (from real life) about themes related to what was just happening in the book. For example, about the organ traffic I mentioned before. It made my experience all the more satisfactory and... disturbing, may I say.<br><br>As this is a final book, I must comment a little on the ending without spoiling it. <b>It was not disappointing.</b> Perhaps a little brighter than I would have wanted, but good nonetheless. It's not entirely enclosing because it leaves room for more story, but it's not so open either.<br><br>In the end, I'm very glad of having tried the first book in this series 4 years ago. It was a long journey, but it was very worth it.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16997868410451944912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1268045032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268045032" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1268045032?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20782933-undivided">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=blur-rating">blur-rating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1268045032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8851977948625215208"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"I love you, Risa," he says. "Every last part of me."</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>Much like all the kids that were unwound in this series, I feel as if I've sold a piece of my soul. Not often do I feel both dragged down and uplifted from the same series, and not often does a book break my nerve to continue on with a genre after finishing. This book and series, while fulfilling all my darkest desires for a climactic series of events, wasn't without it's deep-rooted flaws, in my opinion. I absolutely adored our</span>
  <span id="freeText8851977948625215208" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>"I love you, Risa," he says. "Every last part of me."</i>
</b><br><br><br>Much like all the kids that were unwound in this series, I feel as if I've sold a piece of my soul. Not often do I feel both dragged down and uplifted from the same series, and not often does a book break my nerve to continue on with a genre after finishing. This book and series, while fulfilling all my darkest desires for a climactic series of events, wasn't without it's deep-rooted flaws, in my opinion. I absolutely adored our three main characters, but, for once, they weren't enough for me to give this final book 5 stars. <br><br><b>To fall asleep, and to wake up with your arm around the only girl you've ever truly loved...<br>...<br>To feel invincible, if only for a fleeting moment...</b><br><br><br>As anyone that follows my reviews religiously knows, I adored a certain boy who was doomed from chapter one, book one. He really wedged himself deep in my heart-it's alarming how much I love him. And I guess that's where my personal struggles lie-While his story was absolutely breathtaking, stunning, steal-your-breath awesome, I can't say I cared much past his or Risa's stories. And I don't think that's necessarily a good thing. <br><br><br><b>There's never been a moment in Connor's life that he could call perfect, but this moment, with his arm numb from being around Risa all night, and his sense of smell overwhelmed by the fragrance of her hair-this moment is the closest to perfection he's ever known.</b><br><br><br>I've been known to skim to get to my fav moments, appearances, etc, <b>shut up</b>, but never so much as to ruin a story or cut it up into pieces. But when the story went to a POV not revolving around Connor and Risa, I found I lost interest completely. I loved Lev, as well, but frikkin' being stuck on that boring ass Rez bored me to tears. Like <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/76190-oh-my-god-who-the-hell-cares-m-W4nV_zpshc77jlcx.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430747019i/14756819.png" alt=" photo 76190-oh-my-god-who-the-hell-cares-m-W4nV_zpshc77jlcx.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don't care-Judge away, Judgies. And Starkey. I hate this kid, so why would I want to read about his stupid resistance-what a moron.<br><br><br><b>There's no telling what her life will be like a day from now, much less a year from now. That's the best argument for living in the moment, but how can you live in the moment when all you want is for the moment to end?</b><br><br><br>Ugh. So, anyway. I don't like over analyzing and hearing about religious fronts for a whole story or being in someone's head I could care less about-and there was a lot of that in the last two books. I still adore this series, just know that there are lots of parts I wish I could have skipped.<br><br><b>Betrayal, redemption, loyalty, and a willingness to give up everything to save someone you love more than yourself.</b> This is what touched me the most-My soul was ripped into shreds and I bawled uncontrollably more than once. So many feels that I can't even begin to explain, my emotions are all over the place. Even as I tried to fall asleep I found myself tossing and turning as I mulled over the conclusion to this deeply disturbing series. <br><br><br><b>As he dives down toward tranq sleep, he takes comfort in the absolute knowledge that Connor Lassiter will soon be going down too-but unlike Argent, Connor will never be getting up.</b><br><br><br>I like to think I am beyond being disturbed when it comes to dystopian, but it turns out I couldn't be more wrong. I may have immensely enjoyed this series to the point of obsession, but I still was so beyond heartbroken and disturbed that it should be considered art. <b>Just because you love something doesn't mean it can't hurt you</b>-and this was exactly the case. And, oh yeah, in case you were wondering....<br><br><b>My cry count:<br>73%-</b> Crocodile tears<br><b>75%-</b>Bawling/sobbing/ripping hair out<br><b>78%-</b>Subtle, accepting tears<br><br>Yeah. So. There ya go. I guess I could say try this series out, but I think my past reviews tout how much I've loved it-it's up to you at this point.<br><br><b>Book one:</b> Absolute favorite/Unforgettable/Everything I want in dystopian<br><b>Book Two:</b> Second favorite <br><b>Book Three:</b> Has it's reasons, but definitely my least favorite<br><b>Book Four:</b> Third Favorite, because reasons<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

<div id="review_733571073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/733571073" />
    <a title="ily " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22496761-ily"><img alt="ily " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599357419p2/22496761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/733571073?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="ily " href="/user/show/22496761-ily">ily </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=legen-wait-for-it-dary">legen-wait-for-it-dary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer733571073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12394542841809972300"><blockquote>
  <i>“Hole..." He grips Risa's hand tighter. "Hole, Risa, hole..." And she smiles "Yes, Connor," she says. "<b>You're whole. You're finally whole</b>.”</i>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407082ra/794778.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Favorite book of the year!</b> Las palabras no pueden expresar el cariño que siento hacia esta serie y sus personajes. Neal Shusterman ha destruido mi corazón, una vez más. Pero yo sabía que este libro iba a doler mucho, que acabaría con mi buen estado de ánimo y me dejaría en depresión. He llorado al leer ciertos libros, al ver esa clase de película</span>
  <span id="freeText12394542841809972300" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Hole..." He grips Risa's hand tighter. "Hole, Risa, hole..." And she smiles "Yes, Connor," she says. "<b>You're whole. You're finally whole</b>.”</i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407082ra/794778.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><b>Favorite book of the year!</b> Las palabras no pueden expresar el cariño que siento hacia esta serie y sus personajes. Neal Shusterman ha destruido mi corazón, una vez más. Pero yo sabía que este libro iba a doler mucho, que acabaría con mi buen estado de ánimo y me dejaría en depresión. He llorado al leer ciertos libros, al ver esa clase de películas particularmente tristes y desgarradoras; pero <i>UnDivided</i> no me hizo llorar. No: <b>este libro me destruyó el corazón y dejó los pedazos restantes en el suelo, para yo verlos.</b> Y es que no pude imaginar otro final para esta serie. Shusterman le ha dado una conclusión sorprendente a sus libros. Connor, Risa y Lev han sufrido mucho, han soportado y vivido cosas que pocos podrían. No esperaba un final de mininos felices volando sobre unicornios púrpura; pero estaría muy enojada si algo malo le pasaba a mis personajes favoritos. Y obtuve ambos: momentos tristes y conmovedores, en donde sólo quería llorar; esperanza, una conclusión llena de luz y posibilidades de un mundo mejor, <b>un mundo sin la desconexión.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414711864ra/11681289.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Describiría a <i>UnDivided</i> como una montaña rusa de emociones, emociones incontrolables una vez que superas las primeras páginas. <b>EL CAPÍTULO CINCUENTA Y CINCO ES LA COSA MÁS DOLOROSA QUE HE LEÍDO.</b><br><br><b>Este libro lo fue todo para mí.</b> Llore como nunca. Grité de frustración en algunas ocasiones. Incluso tuve que parar de leer y tomar algo de aire, porque todo era demasiado doloroso y estaba a punto de tener un colapso nervioso. No crean que es una exageración, porque así fue toda mi lectura. <b>Pero eso es lo que amo de leer: llorar, reír y sufrir con los personajes como si yo misma estuviera junto a ellos.</b> Y Neal Shusterman ha logrado todo eso con sus libros. Es difícil decirle adiós a una serie que ha significado tanto para mí. (Me estoy poniendo triste.) Pero sé que Connor, Risa y Lev -aquellos personajes que comenzaron como desconectados fugitivos pero terminaron cambiando el futuro de toda una nación- siempre tendrán un lugar muy especial en mi corazón. <br><br>Gracias, gracias y gracias a Neal Shusterman por haber creado estos magníficos libros. Y, para aquellos que no han leído <i>Unwind:</i> dejen todo lo que están haciendo y léanlo, porque les aseguro que les gustará. (Eso espero.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12394542841809972300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1164584304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1164584304" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1164584304?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Marie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Marie " href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie">Ashley Marie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=might-have-cried">might-have-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=i-own-it">i-own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=freaked-me-the-hell-out">freaked-me-the-hell-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=book-hangover-like-whoa">book-hangover-like-whoa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1164584304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13220471415529447366">UPDATE: Okay is it just me or does this seem weird? I'm one of those people who likes my series books to match -- format, height, covers, etc. And I've waited a year for this one to come out in paperback so it would match the rest of my set (I'm usually not a fan of having all but one or two books in pb vs hb/vice-versa), except that now I come to find out that the paperback edition of this is with the newer cover, with UN in huge letters and then "divided" beneath it. No more Statue of Liberty </span>
  <span id="freeText13220471415529447366" style="display:none">UPDATE: Okay is it just me or does this seem weird? I'm one of those people who likes my series books to match -- format, height, covers, etc. And I've waited a year for this one to come out in paperback so it would match the rest of my set (I'm usually not a fan of having all but one or two books in pb vs hb/vice-versa), except that now I come to find out that the paperback edition of this is with the newer cover, with UN in huge letters and then "divided" beneath it. No more Statue of Liberty arm, no more purple cover. wtf. Why would they do this to me?? Guess I'll just get the hardback and be okay with that. /cries<br /><br /><br /><br />4.5-5 stars<br />Stayed up til 1am reading<br />I am broke<br /><br /><br />-----<br /><br />Just realized I never wrote a review for this. Doing my best to rack my brain so I can say something other than *flails*<br /><br />This book felt like a great ending to a really edgy series. That's not nearly adequate as far as explanations go, but to be honest UnDivided pulled the same thing on me. That is, it left me with quite a few questions regarding certain characters and not a lot of closure. Don't get me wrong, I wasn't expecting to sit there and see through the entire reconstruction process that we *know* has to happen by the end, but we are left with so many loose ends as far as the characters go. What happened to Hayden, and Cam, and Connor, and Bam, and Grace, and Lev... basically I need an epilogue. Or UnBound needs to come out already.<br /><br />Bottom line: this book is insanely good and if you're a fan of the dystopian genre and haven't read this series yet you are missing out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13220471415529447366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1856607125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856607125" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856607125?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25571000-undivided">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=dystopians">dystopians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=yawwwwn">yawwwwn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=why-would-ya">why-would-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=destroy-it-like-a-horcrux">destroy-it-like-a-horcrux</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=gouge-out-my-eyes-with-a-spoon">gouge-out-my-eyes-with-a-spoon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856607125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2674153989929691249"><br/><br/>Undivided is the last book of the UnWind series. By the time all was said and done I was completely uninvested in these characters. What started out so strongly ended so poorly. <br/><br/>Our cast of characters have lost sight of who they are. And, like the previous installment, they are indecisive and spread out all over the place. We get an additional 14 side story lines that seemingly came out of nowhere to add plenty of confusion to the storyline.<br/><br/>Lev’s whole storyline just drove me nuts. It was great </span>
  <span id="freeText2674153989929691249" style="display:none"><br /><br />Undivided is the last book of the UnWind series. By the time all was said and done I was completely uninvested in these characters. What started out so strongly ended so poorly. <br /><br />Our cast of characters have lost sight of who they are. And, like the previous installment, they are indecisive and spread out all over the place. We get an additional 14 side story lines that seemingly came out of nowhere to add plenty of confusion to the storyline.<br /><br />Lev’s whole storyline just drove me nuts. It was great in the beginning to see someone who was brainwashed into believing that being unwound is a holy experience. But where his story went from there was just….UGH. I can’t even come up with a word that explains it well enough! Lame? Overdone? Desperate? Pathetic? I think, honestly, given where the story goes, Lev should have just been killed off in book 2. I just did not fucking care about anything he had going on past the first book. <br /><br />Risa and Connor are supposed to be madly in love with one another. We are told this repeatedly throughout the book. But I just didn't feel it. Some authors are WONDERFUL at creating relationships that feel real. You read these couples and know that they belong together. You are reminded of your hormonal teenage years where LOVE was everything and there was nothing in the world that could stop it. This romance was forced and just did NOT work. <br /><br />All the side characters seemed to be distracting to the whole storyline. I feel like the author meant to use them as a way to tell a broader story, but it just didn't work. They were either underdeveloped, thrown in last minute or so overdone you weren't sure what the REAL storyline was. <br /><br />The ending of the series did very little for me. I just thought there were aspects that could have been done better, and a LOT of things that could have been left out completely. It felt like things were thrown in as an afterthought and it just did NOT work for me. It makes me sad because as you all know, I just <b>love</b> YA Dystopians. (I also feel bad because my dear friend Ashley recommended these to me and I always hate when I don’t jive with a book a friend recommends.) Overall the series would get a 3 star rating from me. I really enjoyed the first two but the last two were HUGE disappointments. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2674153989929691249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1401584535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1401584535" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1401584535?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23206148-terence?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401584535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4214798018007678586">Proactive Citizenry has finally revealed why Cam was created. To make an army of rewound teens for the military. The group has also suppressed technology that would render unwinding obsolete. Connor, Risa, Lev, and Cam struggle to stop unwinding and Proactive Citizenry while bringing the suppressed technology to the surface.<br/><br/>UnDivided was a satisfying conclusion to the Unwind dystology. It kept me in a nervous excited state that compelled me to keep reading until I finished it. The overall blind </span>
  <span id="freeText4214798018007678586" style="display:none">Proactive Citizenry has finally revealed why Cam was created. To make an army of rewound teens for the military. The group has also suppressed technology that would render unwinding obsolete. Connor, Risa, Lev, and Cam struggle to stop unwinding and Proactive Citizenry while bringing the suppressed technology to the surface.<br /><br />UnDivided was a satisfying conclusion to the Unwind dystology. It kept me in a nervous excited state that compelled me to keep reading until I finished it. The overall blind heartlessness of the world surprisingly still shocked me. It's terrifying to fathom that people could care so little about the atrocities going on around them, but it's unfortunately all too similar to the world today.<br /><br />One of my favorite parts of this book and the series as a whole was the thick sense of desperation I felt when reading the book. Clearly it's easy to see why teens would be so desperate when almost the entire world wants them for their body parts. I still can't imagine in a normal setting how a parent could sign their child's life away. I can't even imagine any person being willing to sign a child away that they raised in the case of the storked children. Now for the poor kids who are wards of the state it's not at all difficult to fathom them simply being viewed as unfortunate <i>budget cuts.</i><br /><br />One part I disliked in UnDivided is it transformed itself into more and more of a dystopia as it took on more tropes like the evil corporation responsible for practically everyone's misery. I enjoyed it more in Unwind when the thought was the world was terrified of teenagers and found a brutally efficient way of dealing with them. That felt more genuine and less like an evil business man, sitting in dim light, at a desk with his fingers steepled, and waiting to laugh maniacally.<br /><br />The other thing that bugged me was Camus Comprix's motives. The character's actions really don't make much sense for the majority of the series and UnDivided isn't really an exception. At this point I almost wish he didn't exist. He didn't really add anything to the story overall outside of showing Proactive Citizenry's lack of ethics, but that had already been firmly established and didn't need further bolstering.<br /><br />UnDivided was a thrilling story of a world I hope never approaches becoming a reality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4214798018007678586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_769166104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/769166104" />
    <a title="Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4588347-marie"><img alt="Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357863580p2/4588347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/769166104?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marie" href="/user/show/4588347-marie">Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588347-marie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588347-marie?shelf=dytopian">dytopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588347-marie?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588347-marie?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588347-marie?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer769166104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10410477145889840022">All that I hoped for and more. <div id="review_1728814132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1728814132" />
    <a title="Jesica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica"><img alt="Jesica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469336667p2/44637869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728814132?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesica" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica">Jesica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728814132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10021991015805230456"><blockquote>“There isn’t one single thing that will end unwinding,” she tells them. “It will take a hodgepodge of random events that come together in just the right way and at just the right time to remind society it’s got a conscience.”</blockquote><br/>Revolution comes with huge sacrifices. My heart ached when I read this book, seeing how much sacrifices must be made to wake people’s conscience up against unwinding. The fight was very hard for the AWOLS and I admit I had my doubts too in the middle of the book. It seemed i</span>
  <span id="freeText10021991015805230456" style="display:none"><blockquote>“There isn’t one single thing that will end unwinding,” she tells them. “It will take a hodgepodge of random events that come together in just the right way and at just the right time to remind society it’s got a conscience.”</blockquote><br />Revolution comes with huge sacrifices. My heart ached when I read this book, seeing how much sacrifices must be made to wake people’s conscience up against unwinding. The fight was very hard for the AWOLS and I admit I had my doubts too in the middle of the book. It seemed impossible. I even got frustrated and throw the book away once. Everytime the situation seemed to get better, all went wrong and became even worse than before. The significant characters were either died/captured/unwound/killed/severely injured/hiding or running for their lives. Well, they were generally out of the fight. This book was like roller coaster. When I started it, I believed that unwind would end soon. Everything seemed so convincing but then bad things happened. Then there’re other plans and other failures. It’s so frustrating and I’d almost believed that they’d failed anyway. The enemies were greater than anyone expected. Unwind now mixed with the military forces and, since it was close to election, politics. I’ve never fond of politics, but those politicians were total idiots. I love how Hayden put it: scary.<br /><blockquote>It somehow seems appropriate to me that Election Day falls so close to Halloween this year, considering some of the measures on the ballot. Voluntary unwinding for cash. Tossing the brains of criminals and unwinding the rest of them. The “three strikes” law that allows the Juvenile Authority to arrest and unwind teenage offenders without parental consent. It certainly feels to me like a trip through the haunted mansion, and not even that unwound witch’s head in the crystal ball can predict where it’s going to end.</blockquote><br />The ending was not all happy, they still have to deal with the collateral damage of unwinding that would lasts years. But the world was healing. It had waken up from it’s darkest nightmare and it’s so heartwarming that after all those horrible things, good things can still happen. It’s a wonderful book to end this series. Worth reading. And quoting from radio free Hayden:<br /><blockquote>Signing off with everyone’s favorite tune. And remember—the truth will keep you whole.</blockquote><br /></span>

<div id="review_2856460507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2856460507" />
    <a title="⋆  yel  ⋆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36155695-yel"><img alt="⋆  yel  ⋆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603643156p2/36155695.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2856460507?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⋆  yel  ⋆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⋆  yel  ⋆" href="/user/show/36155695-yel">⋆  yel  ⋆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2856460507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10241829649918397678"><b>
  <i> 5 of 5 stars<br/><br/>----- </i>
</b><br/><br/>If I can only have a short expression to show the overall impact this series gave me:<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Nice socks!"</i>
</b><br/><br/>I can't even begin to describe how satisfied I am with this series. This book, UnDivided, was one of the best concluding novel in a series I have ever read, and most definitely my most favorite in this series. I loved this book so so so freaking much. And I am so damn happy to have a chance to read this gem.<br/><br/>Honestly, I felt anxious starting this book. Not because the concl</span>
  <span id="freeText10241829649918397678" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> 5 of 5 stars<br /><br />----- </i>
</b><br /><br />If I can only have a short expression to show the overall impact this series gave me:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Nice socks!"</i>
</b><br /><br />I can't even begin to describe how satisfied I am with this series. This book, UnDivided, was one of the best concluding novel in a series I have ever read, and most definitely my most favorite in this series. I loved this book so so so freaking much. And I am so damn happy to have a chance to read this gem.<br /><br />Honestly, I felt anxious starting this book. Not because the conclusion might not reach my expectation, but because I have no freaking idea how Neal Shusterman would end this wonderful series. And also it was kind of sad saying goodbye to these characters that I came to love. There was even a part of me wanting to hold off reading this book because I just don't want this series to end. But despite everything, my excitement over what was going to happen can't be beaten.<br /><br />This series was so unpredictable. You think you knew where it was going but then it would take a sudden turn that would make your head spin. It can also easily get you at the edge of your seat.This was so so so good.<br /><br />All characters were not a waste. I respect even the most evil villain of them because of how great they portray their wickedness. They were so infuriating but they were so damn good at it they deserved my praise. Starkey, Nelson and Roberta, they made the story a color of blood with their viciousness. Even the redeeming antagonists like Argent and Bam, they made me want to salute them with their last minute redemption that was done in their own way. The supporting characters like Cam, Hayden, Grace, Sonia, Miracolina, Una, the Admiral (with his sudden appearance) who made their success possible. <br /><br />And most especially the main protagonists who suffered a lot more than one individual can bear in a lifetime; Connor Lassiter, Risa Ward and Lev Calder (Lev Tashi'ne). Damn, they sure suffered a lot. Maybe it seemed impossible that teenagers like them can overthrow a disastrous Unwind Accord, but they still managed to do it. With their anger and desperation, combined with their wits and strong will to survive and the hope of a future without unwinding, their age didn't even matter to be able to achieve their success.<br /><br />But what I admire the most in this story is how they were able to win against a lot of enemies that held different agendas to overpower them. They became a team, but they were not necessarily piled together to do that. They became a team, with different roles to play, different directions to turn, different decisions to make and different destinations to end up and all of them were spread all throughout the story. <i>"They all have jobs to do and they need to do it in their own way",</i>I can practically hear the author says. They encountered countless of problems along the way and Neal Shusterman made it look like they were fighting their own battle, as if they were involuntarily assigned with their own problems to solve, but in a bigger picture, they were actually running towards one goal. The author played it out by having different perspective to show that and I don't think there's a better way to do it. It was so damn perfect!<br /><br />Aside from the plot itself and the spectacular character development, I so loved the strategic style of this series, the realistic approach in this dystopian world. Given that most of the characters were teenagers, it was not impossible to believe about their capabilities to do what they did to succeed. <br /><br />I mentioned that this probably is my favorite book in this series but seriously, I loved every single book. If I am to read this series again, and I am positive I will, I know that the first three books, which I initially gave 4-star ratings, have a high possibility to have a higher rating, maybe a 5-star rating as well just like this one. I just loved this so so much and this just became one of my most favorite series of all time. Highly, highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10241829649918397678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
